Not just hikers to other hikers, but the townspeople in each of the crossing areas literally come out to the trail to feed and take care of the hikers. Even with all of the scary stories, there's truly so much "magic" (as it's called out there) and kindness. Met a guy that lived out there on the trail because he too felt it was home, and lived on the kindness of hikers. Thankfully I met him in full daylight with lots of other hikers around and I did give him some food. Still best to keep your wits about you and never truly let your guard down, just in case. Or as mad-eye-moody would say, "constant vigilance."

Aside from accidents, wild animals or even just natural causes that may put you into an emergency situation, there are also mentally deranged people out in the woods, where many like to hide. Not everyone living away from society is a psychopath. Some just like the peace and quiet. But that doesn't mean there aren't any psychopaths living out there either. And for those psychopaths who do dwell off the grid, for a lone camper, hiker, etc. If they find you, and their intent is a violent one, they're able to do what they want with you and no one is going to know anything is wrong with you until you're reported overdue to return from your little solitary adventure. You go out there to do that stuff, you're far better off with a big group. Alone you're a sitting duck. I think it's stupid to venture off alone in the wild. Even with just 2 of you, that's not great odds either. Especially 2 women or a man and a woman. 2 guys are going to fare better most of the time, I know that people will say that sounds sexist and I don't care. It's time to get real about this. Violence against women is so incredibly high in this country. For the majority of predators, a woman is who they're looking for which is going to force women to take measures to protect themselves and I'm sorry, heading out certain places alone as a woman is just stupid. I get so upset when my wife does that crap. She's so stubborn, like most independent people. But damn it, there's being independent and then there's being stupid. Some of the risks she's taken have just been stupid and careless and makes my stomach upset knowing that these deranged animals are lurking in plain sight most of the time. It's ok for women to not be so polite to strange men who approach you. Screw his feelings, read "The Gift of Fear." And take the authors advice and warnings VERY seriously. Well, besides the obvious that it can see what is underground - the machine is fairly light and now it has a tablet computer that you attach to it and the tablet records everything to an SD card (like a 512GB card). It is supposed to be accurate down to a millimeter squared area. Now - does this mean a skeleton would just pop out? No. What it means is that instead of having to go through by hand through (I don't know - a mile maybe) the ground digging everything up - instead, you just do the walk through, it keeps the logarithmic location of where you are AND when you examine the map - it can tell you exactly where you were standing. (And not by going "There you are!") So then you can just go to that location and dig. Also, the police could use the new Lidar they are using to see ancient cities in the Amazon even though the cities are covered by dense forest. So they can find interesting places to examine - or - then take the ground penetrating radar unit to that location and walk around on it to get a better view of what is there. A few days ago,  I decided to give "Run, Fool!" a shot, and I have not put it down. Whenever I'm in my car, or playing games, or cleaning, I've been listening to Rodney Barnes tell stories. 17 episodes in, and I can't wait for the next one. I first read about this case in one of my favorite books 'A walk in the woods' by Bill Bryson. It's an amazing book about his attempt to hike the Appalachian trail as a middle aged unfit first time hiker along with his friend who only admits that he is an alcoholic when it's too late to do anything about it as they are literally in the middle of nowhere. Overall it's a lighthearted funny book which only made the chapter about this even more shocking. There was two other stories in the book that have stayed with me the first was about a random dude who just went for a short hike in the woods close to his house and the Appalachian trail of course but as he is a local and isn't actually hiking the trail he goes off trail through the woods when he comes across a small aeroplane that had obviously crashed into the woods and never been discovered, the skeletal remains of the pilot and one other was still strapped into the seats but in the back of the plane was millions of dollars and a huge amount of cocaine! It turned out the plane had sat there for around six years with nobody any the wiser, it was theorised that the pilot had disconnected the transponder and flown extremely low to avoid detection which is why there was no huge search party searching for the plane and it's occupants. Very quickly the other story was in a chapter describing animal attacks on the trail from when it opened right up to the year he wrote the book. So this guy got up in the middle of the night and headed to the trees to relieve himself but out of nowhere a huge owl swooped down and attacked his head with it's incredibly strong & sharp talons which resulted in the poor man being scalped, the owl flew off with all of his hair and a very large section of skin from the man's head. One more thing although they have made a movie from this book it is nothing even close to the book they went for cheap jokes and laughs and cut out all of the historical facts including every animal attack, violence or anything that could be considered adult material.

9:45 hippy meets hill-billies. (I'm generalizing) When I go in the the mountains, If you stay near road camping sites, you get a mix of hippies and hill-billies. The campsites closer to civilization are mostly hill-billies: glass, garbage, cans with gun shots in them (kids partying too). The further you go, the more hippy the campsites become: no trash, nature. But anything accessible by road can have-hillbilly traces at it. If you want true hippy places, you have to get off the roads. Backpacking is nearly 100% hippy (maybe some horse people). The only way to avoid people, is to get off the roads. I've gone to the furthest roads of the largest wilderness in the lower 48, (90 miles from nearest gas station), and there are still old people RV'ing up there. Or you can find a rough road that goes up some pass, and you will get mostly Jeepers/Hunters (classy hill-billies).

The US justice system is far better than the majority of the world although it's far from perfect. Using this case as a yardstick to measure and condemn the system is a mistake.  First off, when Smith murdered the two hikers in 1981 he was sentenced to two 15 year terms. Unfortunately they ran concurrently so he had to be released after 15 years instead of 30.   However he was required to be on probation for a decade, including wearing an electronic ankle monitor until 2006.  The fact that he served 15 years in prison and then another 10 on supervised probation yet neither law enforcement or a mental health professional was able to suss out that he was a serial killer and probably incapable of rehabilitation seems like the real issue.   As soon as Smith was no longer being monitored in 2006 he left his mother's house and moved out to the A.T. where he attacked these men and probably was responsible for the death of others.   The state laws where Smith was tried and convicted in 1981 required that he be released after 15 years, although he was on supervised probation. During that time he didn't commit any crimes that the police are aware of.   State laws, like federal laws, are a reflection of the political reality in each particular state. If Smith hadn't been up for parole or if he hadn't served his two sentences concurrently he would have still been in jail in 2006.   People often react to stories like this by saying "the system is broken" despite the fact that the US has more people incarcerated per capita than any other country but China.   The US justice system definitely has serious issues but i would still prefer it over 90% of the countries on the planet.  The main reason our incarceration rate is so high is the decades long failed "war on drugs" and the politically motivated mandatory sentencing, like the 3 strikes rule.  In some states these measures are being rolled back and the war on drugs is spending more on recovery and intervention and less on incarceration.

I have several chilling camping stories. And yes Mr Ballen can use them. Let me know if you need more detail.   1. Human vs human (less exciting but was still scary) My husband, daughter and I went camping. My daughter was young, very young. I won't disclose how young to avoid the comments about her being too young and taking away from the points. We set up off a back road that led into the mountains. It's called Truck Road out Butte Falls, Oregon. It leads up into the woods and even pops out on major roads if I remember right.   Anyway we get our tent and easy up set up and start enjoying our time. Everything seems normal, quiet. Peaceful. We made dinner and went to bed.   At almost 5am we had to get up to take my daughter outside to use bathroom. My husband turns the lanterns on in easy up next to tent so we can see.  We were laying back down and I hear a vehicle coming. We had been out here a few times before and rarely seen vehicles but it does pop out and lead else where so it could have been a hunter or even law enforcement so we quietly listen for how close the vehicle is approaching.   We were camped around a little raised pull off that over looked the main road so we could see down where the vehicle was. The vehicle started honking and a man yelled something we couldn't understand. My husband armed himself and we waited to see what the man in vehicle would do.   The vehicle left. Did not approach. So it wasn't law enforcement, law enforcement would have checked in with us.   We were beyond creeped out and this sense of unease was overwhelming, too many unknowns. Who was this man? Why did he honk and holler then leave? Not that I wanted him to come closer, BUT WHAT WAS HIS POINT?   When I come across campers I turn around and leave quietly. I don't make myself known at 5am by being obnoxious.   I our my daughter in truck, then We loaded up all of our camp gear in like 20 minutes. Maybe less. We were scared. Armed, but scared. Our gun safe doesn't fit all of our weapons but we didn't know who this person was or why they had found our camp spot or what they wanted so bad to be as noisy as they were.   Husband and I climb into his lifted ford and THE VEHICLE CAME BACK!!!!! As we climbed in- the vehicle approached. Was the same one. Dark 4 door car. It was just light enough when it came by first time at 5am to make out if color was light or dark and what kind of car, like we could tell the silhouette was dar and an suv, it wasn't a tiny car or truck.   The car was different this time. It had 3 other people in it. Men it looked like. We didn't get a super close look of who was in vehicle like individuals faces but it was 4 decent sized people in it so they were at least adults if not all men.   I told my husband to pick up his speed and drive towards the car. If the car didn't move to allow us to pass:, hit it with our lifted truck. Truck is lifted enough that an impact with car would have damaged our bumper and wench but that's it, we'd be driving away and they wouldn't. The car was blocking the only way to get on the main road from our raised pull off. As we picked up speed the car backed up suddenly turned around and left, going quick enough to kick up dust and block us from seeing the license plate. We would have had to have gotten super close to see it and we didn't want to interact we simply wanted out of the situation.   What did these men want? Why did one guy holler at us then leave and bring back 3 more men? What would have happened to us if we went back to sleep instead of leaving as quickly as we did? Did making the knee jerk reaction we did save our lives? I don't know the answers and never will, mostly thankful. I just hope these men didn't harm other campers who were innocently enjoying nature.     2. Human vs unknown (mini stories as there are 3 id like to share)  A.) The white dress lady. (Most recent) Last fall upon leaving one of our favorite swim spots in the woods at a fairly used spot, it was starting to get dark but not fully dark. We exited the little road that led to swim spots and camp spots when my daughter asked if I seen the lady in the white dress.  I said no but my husband said "you seen that too?" to my daughter. I said "seen what?" My daughter said there was a lady standing by the tree In a white dress but she couldn't see her face and she didn't wave back at her(daughter). I didn't notice it but both my daughter and husband did.  My husband asked if I wanted to go back and my stomach knotted and I told him we cannot help her right now... pretty sure it was a ghost or spirit or something not really there but still there...  B) "The rock" We found a new area on Google maps and went to explore it (DO NOT DO THIS IF YOU ARE UNPREPARED TO SURVIVE IF YOU GET STUCK SOME WHERE AS GOOGLE MAPS DOESNT SHOW 100% OF CHANGES OR ISSUES WITH THE ROADS).  Husband and I pull into this pull off camp site and explore it for a few minutes to stretch our legs. The water that should have been there was dried up that time of year so we didn't want to stay long was hot and we were looking for a place to cool off. After a half hour or so if hanging out at this spot we decided to load out kids up, son and daughter. Husband was changing my son inside the car and my daughter was running on the driver's side of the car in front of me. Everything was normal but I had a feeling of being watched. However no other cars were around so I figured maybe a deer was watching us or something and my sense of unease was just misplaced.   Then, I felt a thud about 2 feet behind me.   EVERYONE I HAD WITH ME WAS IN FRONT OF ME. Husband was about 4 feet away changing my son and my daughter was about the same distance but like to the left not right by the car.   I 100% felt something behind me, one thud. Felt the vibrations in my feet.   I look behind me and this rock is laying there than I hadn't noticed before. Not that I notice every rock or stick but this rock was foot ball sized and I had just walked from that direction and the rock would have been a rock I would have seen.   I told my husband we needed to leave and I mist have been white as a ghost or something because he rushed to finish my son and loaded my daughter quick. I didn't move until my daughter was in the car.   I'm 80% certain something threw the rock and it landed 2 feet behind me, like if I backed up a big step I would have tripped over the rock. It was that close. And if something didn't throw the rock, then I cannot explain the thud I felt in both feet but no one else noticed.   Why, and what, would throw the rock?   Last one I'll share for now: C.) The scream Husband kids and I went to have a cook out in the woods. We found a camp ground that was closed that time of year for some reason maybe government shut down? Not sure. Anyways we drug out the food and made burgers and hot dogs and we ate and had a good time. As it started to get dark we loaded up the kids then I started to help my husband load the food while he went to get water from the creek nearby, maybe 50 feet away. After he disappeared I again felt the unease of being watched. I had loaded everything other than my husband's stuff he would grab in a second when he returned with water so I got inside the car with kids. My daughter said it was cold so I turned car on and turned on heater. Then I heard the loudest, high pitched scream I've ever heard. Almost like a banshee from mass effect 3. (Look it up)  I locked the doors and looked at my daughter who didn't seem as scared as I did so I just sat there watching for my husband to come back with the water. He finally did like 30 seconds later although it felt like an eternity. I asked if he heard anything while getting water and he said no. And he looked at me and said "I'm guessing you did?" So I explained it and he re locked the doors and we drove home.   Is it possible to hear a warning from someone or something without an actual noise being made others can hear? I know I heard something. But no-one else did...     I'm terrified of the woods but I don't want to stop living my life. I haven't gone camping since the first part of comment we just do day trips to places. But now even that feels uneasy. I want to find my peace in nature but unsure what that would take. Not even sure if I can. Weird things happen out there I cannot explain. Seems like once every dozen trips out something will happen that isn't a good feeling...

As someone who hikes a lot, this is something I'm always wary of. I carry a 7" blade with me on most hikes, both because a lot of people feed the bears so they're somewhat likely to approach people, and because the Appalachians are a great place to hide if you're doing sketchy shit. I've only ever hiked the TN and NC part of the range, but I've definitely seen some shit out there. Be aware of your surroundings and the behaviors of other people near you no matter where you are, but especially when you're someplace isolated. It could save your life.

I'm trying to think of how that experience would be - running into strangers on the Appalachian Trail... I've spent my entire life in Arkansas where we have a lot of hiking trails, creeks and camping sites and such - probably nothing compared to the Appalachian Trail - but a lot of beautiful, pristine, primitive and highly popular places - and there was dozens of times, if not more, that I would be swimming, fishing, kayaking or hiking alone and/or camping alone or with a small group and a random person/people/group would just walk up and hang out - sometimes it would be very..."rough" looking folks just stumbling out of the dark and they'd just sit and get drunk and laugh and tell stories with us.   Sometimes maybe I would know them (since we always camped close to where _I_ grew up and most of my friends were from farther away) and sometimes I wouldn't. Sometimes, they'd be a long haired mountain man, moonshiner or meth cook and other times they'd be a tweaked out meth zombie - sometimes all of the above.   The point I'm trying to make is, I was never just _horrified_ or anything when someone would walk up on me/us - and these sites were actually fairly popular for the area - again, probably a miniscule number of visitors compared to the AT but - specifically with our favorite creek - Snow Creek - a dirt road running beside a pretty big creek - some might even say "a river" in some areas - with primitive, non-official campsites lining the dirt road periodically maintained by just us people and kept trampled down by our traffic - I remember very often, we'd go to camp, swim, fish, canoe/kayak, etc., and all probably dozen campsites would be packed with RVs ( _nobody_ from my area owned an RV) and the few times we'd just squeeze on in for creek access, they'd all be from either far out of town or even out of state.   I remember we would always shoot guns up there - and we packed some wild heat - it probably sounded like a warzone. There was this one time where a big RV was in "our spot" and they seemed cool so we squeezed by and went down to the creek and, we were stupid-ass kids, weren't considerate _at all_ , we didn't think about it, figured the RV people were probably cool, thought we were far enough away, etc. and we started blasting our guns at the creek (like I think I had my Mosin Nagant (probably the loudest of our guns), my friend probably had his AK and 12 gauge, and maybe somebody had a pistol or whatever and maybe some .22's) - like typical firepower for this area but likely terrifying insanity and overkill for anyone from out of town (turned out they were from the state but were "city slickers" lol).   So they almost immediately called the cops on us and several state troopers rolled up on us. We both told our stories and the state troopers told the RV people we had every right to shoot guns where we were shooting - it was based on the distance from the road and the distance from the RV or something - and my wise-ass, overly aggressive, in-your-face type of friend made absolutely certain to shake the state troopers' hands right in front of the RV people, converse with them and thank them before they left and we continued shooting - as the RV left to go to another spot...   I feel like we were sort of in the wrong just like ethically/morally even if it wasn't illegal - it was just a younger dude (15ish years older than us - we were late-teens/early 20's), his wife and a kid or two... So I think we were the "scary, dangerous people" that day... My friend was always kind of the "leader" or whatever just because he was so aggressive (always wanted to start crap with people or scare them or whatever - we thought it was hilarious at the time) and he's the one who insisted we stop in that exact spot and start shooting even though the RV was there - he ended up being an MP in the military and then a police officer.   I remember this redneck dude asked to shoot his AK one time and he just looked at him and was like "Noop". Lol.. The redneck got so mad he had his fists clenched and was rocking back and forth, red-faced and was even kind of crying from rage - like about to jump my friend - even though there was 3 of us with guns - and my friend was just taunting him - like, "Why are you crying you bitch?"... So we were 100% the assholes a lot of times back in those days.

There are trail angels that leave food in drop boxes. Boxes made from wood with a latch type lid. These boxes are usually attached to trees along the trail. The trail angels are locals from the little towns that run along the trail.  Maybe the food boxes that Ricky found were empty. Hence the reason he was starving. If Ricky and his dog would have made it to these little towns then he would have gotten homemade meals,a shower,and a nights stay away from the trail. These towns take in long term hikers whenever a storm or hard rain or snow coming. Churches open their doors and trail hostels are open during bad weather so hikers can get away from bad weather and get a hot meal served and a hot shower. These places will have a log book so in case something happens to a hiker the authorities will have some kind of sighting of hiker.
